        <td>
         612/km
         <sup>
          2
         </sup>
         (1,585.1/sq mi) (
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_territories_by_population_density" title="List of countries and territories by population density">
          22nd
         </a>
         )
        </td>
       </tr>

         </a>

      <p>
       <b>
        Aruba
       </b>
       (
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'r' in 'rye'">
            r
           </span>
           <span title="/uː/: 'oo' in 'goose'">
            uː
           </span>
           <span title="'b' in 'buy'">
            b
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key">
        <i title="English pronunciation respelling">
         ə-
         <span style="font-size:90%">
          ROO
         </span>
         -bə
        </i>
       </a>
       ;
       <small>
        Dutch:
       </small>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Dutch" title="Help:IPA/Dutch">
         [aːˈrubaː]
        </a>
       </span>
       ) is an island and a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Countries_of_the_Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Countries of the Kingdom of the Netherlands">
        constituent country
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">
        Kingdom of the Netherlands
       </a>
       in the southern
       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">
        Caribbean Sea
       </a>
       , located about 1,600 kilometres (990 mi) west of the main part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">
        Lesser Antilles
       </a>
       and 29 kilometres (18 mi)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Britannica_5-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Britannica-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       north of the coast of
       <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">
        Venezuela
       </a>
       . It measures 32 kilometres (20 mi) long from its northwestern to its southeastern end and 10 kilometres (6 mi) across at its widest point.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Britannica_5-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Britannica-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Together with
       <a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">
        Bonaire
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Curaçao">
        Curaçao
       </a>
       , Aruba forms a group referred to as the
       <a href="/wiki/ABC_islands_(Lesser_Antilles)" title="ABC islands (Lesser Antilles)">
        ABC islands
       </a>
       . Collectively, Aruba and the other Dutch islands in the Caribbean are often called the
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Caribbean" title="Dutch Caribbean">
        Dutch Caribbean
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Aruba is one of the four countries that form the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">
        Kingdom of the Netherlands
       </a>
       , along with the
       <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">
        Netherlands
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Curaçao">
        Curaçao
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Sint_Maarten" title="Sint Maarten">
        Sint Maarten
       </a>
       ; the citizens of these countries are all Dutch nationals. Aruba has no administrative subdivisions, but, for census purposes, is divided into eight regions. Its capital is
       <a href="/wiki/Oranjestad,_Aruba" title="Oranjestad, Aruba">
        Oranjestad
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Unlike much of the Caribbean region, Aruba has a dry climate and an arid,
       <a href="/wiki/Cactus" title="Cactus">
        cactus
       </a>
       -strewn landscape. This climate has helped tourism as visitors to the island can reliably expect warm, sunny weather. It has a land area of 179 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (69.1 sq mi) and is densely populated, with a total of 102,484 inhabitants at the 2010 Census. It lies outside
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Alley" title="Hurricane Alley">
        Hurricane Alley
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aruba&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Aruba" title="History of Aruba">
        History of Aruba
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Oranjestad.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1359" data-file-width="2184" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Oranjestad.jpg/220px-Oranjestad.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Oranjestad.jpg/330px-Oranjestad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Oranjestad.jpg/440px-Oranjestad.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Oranjestad.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The capital,
         <a href="/wiki/Oranjestad,_Aruba" title="Oranjestad, Aruba">
          Oranjestad
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Aruba's first inhabitants are thought to have been
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caquetios_Indian" title="Caquetios Indian">
        Caquetío Amerindians
       </a>
       from the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arawak_peoples" title="Arawak peoples">
        Arawak
       </a>
       tribe, who migrated there from
       <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">
        Venezuela
       </a>
       to escape attacks by the
       <a href="/wiki/Kalina_people" title="Kalina people">
        Caribs
       </a>
       . Fragments of the earliest known Indian settlements date back to 1000 AD. As sea currents made
       <a href="/wiki/Canoe" title="Canoe">
        canoe
       </a>
       travel to other
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caribbean_islands" title="Caribbean islands">
        Caribbean islands
       </a>
       difficult,
       <a href="/wiki/Caquetio" title="Caquetio">
        Caquetio
       </a>
       culture remained more closely associated with that of mainland South America.
      </p>
      <p>
       Europeans first learned of Aruba following the explorations for Spain by
       <a href="/wiki/Amerigo_Vespucci" title="Amerigo Vespucci">
        Amerigo Vespucci
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Alonso_de_Ojeda" title="Alonso de Ojeda">
        Alonso de Ojeda
       </a>
       in the summer of 1499. Both described Aruba as an "island of giants", remarking on the comparatively large stature of the native Caquetíos compared to Europeans. Gold was not discovered on Aruba for another 300 years. Vespucci returned to Spain with stocks of cotton and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caesalpinia_echinata" title="Caesalpinia echinata">
        brazilwood
       </a>
       from the island and described houses built into the ocean. Vespucci and Ojeda's tales spurred interest in Aruba, and Spaniards soon colonized the island.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-advent_6-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-advent-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-early_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-early-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Because it had low rainfall, Aruba was not considered profitable for the plantation system and the economics of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave_trade" title="Slave trade">
        slave trade
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Aruba was colonized by
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">
        Spain
       </a>
       for over a century.
       <i>
        Simas
       </i>
       , the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Cacique" title="Cacique">
         Cacique
        </a>
       </i>
       , or
       <a href="/wiki/Tribal_chief" title="Tribal chief">
        chief
       </a>
       , in Aruba, welcomed the first Catholic priests in Aruba, who gave him a wooden cross as a gift. In 1508, the Spanish Crown appointed Alonso de Ojeda as its first Governor of Aruba, as part of
       <i>
        Nueva Andalucía
       </i>
       . Arawaks spoke the "broken Spanish" which their ancestors had learned on
       <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">
        Hispaniola
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Another governor appointed by Spain was
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Mart%C3%ADnez_de_Ampi%C3%A9s" title="Juan Martínez de Ampiés">
        Juan Martínez de Ampiés
       </a>
       . A
       <i>
        cédula real
       </i>
       decreed in November 1525 gave Ampiés, factor of Española, the right to repopulate Aruba. In 1528, Ampiés was replaced by a representative of the
       <a href="/wiki/Welser" title="Welser">
        House of Welser
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Augsburg" title="Augsburg">
        Augsburg
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">
        Dutch
       </a>
       statutes have applied to Aruba since 1629.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (July 2015)">
           clarification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The Netherlands acquired Aruba in 1636. Since 1636, Aruba has been under
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">
        Dutch
       </a>
       administration, initially governed by
       <a href="/wiki/Peter_Stuyvesant" title="Peter Stuyvesant">
        Peter Stuyvesant
       </a>
       , later appointed to
       <a href="/wiki/New_Amsterdam" title="New Amsterdam">
        New Amsterdam
       </a>
       (New York City). Stuyvesant was on a special mission in Aruba in November and December 1642. The island was included under the
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_West_India_Company" title="Dutch West India Company">
        Dutch West India Company
       </a>
       (W.I.C.) administration, as "New Netherland and Curaçao", from 1648 to 1664. In 1667 the Dutch administration appointed an Irishman as "Commandeur" in Aruba.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Dutch took control 135 years after the Spanish, leaving the Arawaks to farm and graze livestock, and used the island as a source of meat for other Dutch possessions in the Caribbean.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="no direct linkage has been supplied to demonstrate that one lead to the other (August 2012)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       During the Napoleonic wars, the
       <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">
        British Empire
       </a>
       took control over the island, between 1799 and 1802, and between 1804 and 1816, before handing it back to the Dutch.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       During World War II with the
       <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_in_World_War_II#German_occupation" title="Netherlands in World War II">
        occupation of the Netherlands
       </a>
       in 1940 the oil facilities in Aruba came under the administration of the
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_government-in-exile" title="Dutch government-in-exile">
        Dutch government-in-exile
       </a>
       in London, and
       <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Aruba" title="Attack on Aruba">
        Aruba continued to supply oil to the British and their allies
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Move_towards_independence">
        Move towards independence
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aruba&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Move towards independence">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <img alt="Ambox current red.svg" data-file-height="290" data-file-width="360" height="34" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" width="42"/>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section's
          <b>
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute">
            factual accuracy
           </a>
           may be compromised due to out-of-date information
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (April 2013)
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       In August 1947, Aruba presented its first
       <i>
        Staatsreglement
       </i>
       (constitution), for Aruba's
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Independence" title="Independence">
         status aparte
        </a>
       </i>
       as an autonomous state within the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">
        Kingdom of the Netherlands
       </a>
       . By 1954, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charter_of_the_Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Charter of the Kingdom of the Netherlands">
        Charter of the Kingdom of the Netherlands
       </a>
       was established, providing a framework for relations between Aruba and the rest of the Kingdom.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1972, at a conference in
       <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">
        Suriname
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Betico_Croes" title="Betico Croes">
        Betico Croes
       </a>
       (MEP), a politician from Aruba, proposed a
       <i>
        sui-generis
       </i>
       Dutch Commonwealth of four states: Aruba, the Netherlands, Suriname and the
       <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Antilles" title="Netherlands Antilles">
        Netherlands Antilles
       </a>
       , each to have its own nationality. C. Yarzagaray, a parliamentary member representing the AVP political party, proposed a
       <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">
        referendum
       </a>
       so that the people of Aruba could choose whether they wanted total independence or
       <i>
        Status Aparte
       </i>
       as a full autonomous state under the Crown.
      </p>
      <p>
       Croes worked in Aruba to inform and prepare the people of Aruba for independence. In 1976, he appointed a committee that chose the national flag and anthem, introducing them as symbols of Aruba's sovereignty and independence. He set 1981 as a target date for independence. In March 1977, the first Referendum for Self Determination was held with the support of the United Nations; 82% of the participants voted for independence.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_Aruba_Profile_10-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-BBC_Aruba_Profile-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Island Government of Aruba assigned the Institute of Social Studies in
       <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">
        The Hague
       </a>
       to prepare a study for independence; it was titled
       <i>
        Aruba en Onafhankelijkheid, achtergronden, modaliteiten en mogelijkheden; een rapport in eerste aanleg
       </i>
       (Aruba and independence, backgrounds, modalities and opportunities; a preliminary report) (1978). At the conference in The Hague in 1981, Aruba's independence was set for the year 1991.
      </p>
      <p>
       In March 1983, Aruba reached an official agreement within the Kingdom for its independence, to be developed in a series of steps as the Crown granted increasing autonomy. In August 1985 Aruba drafted a constitution that was unanimously approved. On 1 January 1986, after elections were held for its first parliament, Aruba seceded from the Netherlands Antilles; it officially became a country of the Kingdom of the Netherlands. Full independence was projected in 1996.
      </p>
      <p>
       After his death in 1986, Croes was proclaimed
       <i>
        Libertador di Aruba
       </i>
       . At a convention in The Hague in 1990, at the request of Aruba's
       <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Oduber" title="Nelson Oduber">
        Prime Minister
       </a>
       , the governments of Aruba, the Netherlands, and the Netherlands Antilles postponed indefinitely its transition to full independence. The article scheduling Aruba's complete independence was rescinded in 1995, although the process could be revived after another referendum.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aruba&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geography">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Aruba" title="Geography of Aruba">
        Geography of Aruba
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aruba_map.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="351" data-file-width="326" height="237" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Aruba_map.png/220px-Aruba_map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1b/Aruba_map.png 1.5x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aruba_map.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A map of Aruba
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aruba_-_Encyclopaedie_van_Nederlandsch_West-Indi%C3%AB-Antilles_part_1,_right.gif">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2422" data-file-width="1971" height="270" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Aruba_-_Encyclopaedie_van_Nederlandsch_West-Indi%C3%AB-Antilles_part_1%2C_right.gif/220px-Aruba_-_Encyclopaedie_van_Nederlandsch_West-Indi%C3%AB-Antilles_part_1%2C_right.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Aruba_-_Encyclopaedie_van_Nederlandsch_West-Indi%C3%AB-Antilles_part_1%2C_right.gif/330px-Aruba_-_Encyclopaedie_van_Nederlandsch_West-Indi%C3%AB-Antilles_part_1%2C_right.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Aruba_-_Encyclopaedie_van_Nederlandsch_West-Indi%C3%AB-Antilles_part_1%2C_right.gif/440px-Aruba_-_Encyclopaedie_van_Nederlandsch_West-Indi%C3%AB-Antilles_part_1%2C_right.gif 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aruba_-_Encyclopaedie_van_Nederlandsch_West-Indi%C3%AB-Antilles_part_1,_right.gif" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map of Aruba from the
         <i>
          <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Encyclopaedie_van_Nederlandsch_West-Indi%C3%AB_1914-1917&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Encyclopaedie van Nederlandsch West-Indië 1914-1917 (page does not exist)">
           Encyclopaedie van Nederlandsch West-Indië 1914-1917
          </a>
          .
         </i>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:197306_aruba_naturalbridge.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1451" data-file-width="2294" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/197306_aruba_naturalbridge.jpg/220px-197306_aruba_naturalbridge.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/197306_aruba_naturalbridge.jpg/330px-197306_aruba_naturalbridge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/197306_aruba_naturalbridge.jpg/440px-197306_aruba_naturalbridge.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:197306_aruba_naturalbridge.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Natural bridge in Aruba (collapsed 2 September 2005)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Aruba is a generally flat, riverless island in the
       <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Antilles" title="Leeward Antilles">
        Leeward Antilles
       </a>
       island arc of the
       <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">
        Lesser Antilles
       </a>
       in the southern part of the Caribbean. It has white sandy beaches on the western and southern coasts of the island, relatively sheltered from fierce ocean currents.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aruba:_the_happy_island_11-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aruba:_the_happy_island-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This is where most tourist development has occurred.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aruba:_the_happy_island_11-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aruba:_the_happy_island-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The northern and eastern coasts, lacking this protection, are considerably more battered by the sea and have been left largely untouched by humans.
      </p>
      <p>
       The hinterland of the island features some rolling hills, the best known of which are called
       <a href="/wiki/Hooiberg" title="Hooiberg">
        Hooiberg
       </a>
       at 165 meters (541 ft) and
       <a href="/wiki/Mount_Jamanota" title="Mount Jamanota">
        Mount Jamanota
       </a>
       , the highest on the island at 188 meters (617 ft) above sea level. Oranjestad, the capital, is located at
       <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion">
        <a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Aruba&amp;params=12_19_N_70_1_W_">
         <span class="geo-default">
          <span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">
           <span class="latitude">
            12°19′N
           </span>
           <span class="longitude">
            70°1′W
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
         <span class="geo-multi-punct">
          ﻿ / ﻿
         </span>
         <span class="geo-nondefault">
          <span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">
           12.317°N 70.017°W
          </span>
          <span style="display:none">
           ﻿ /
           <span class="geo">
            12.317; -70.017
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
        </a>
       </span>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       To the east of Aruba are
       <a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">
        Bonaire
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Curaçao">
        Curaçao
       </a>
       , two island territories which once formed the southwest part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Antilles" title="Netherlands Antilles">
        Netherlands Antilles
       </a>
       . This group of islands is sometimes called the
       <a href="/wiki/ABC_islands_(Lesser_Antilles)" title="ABC islands (Lesser Antilles)">
        ABC islands
       </a>
       . They are located on the South American
       <a href="/wiki/Continental_shelf" title="Continental shelf">
        continental shelf
       </a>
       and therefore geographically listed as part of South America.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Aruba_Natural_Bridge" title="Aruba Natural Bridge">
        Natural Bridge
       </a>
       was a large, naturally formed limestone bridge on the island's north shore. It was a popular tourist destination until its collapse in 2005.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cities_and_towns">
        Cities and towns
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aruba&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Cities and towns">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Aruba" title="List of cities in Aruba">
        List of cities in Aruba
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The island, with a population of just over 100,000 inhabitants, does not have major cities. However, most of the island's population resides in or surrounding the two major city-like districts of Oranjestad (Capital) and San Nicolaas. Furthermore, the island is divided into six districts, which are:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Noord" title="Noord">
         Noord
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Oranjestad,_Aruba" title="Oranjestad, Aruba">
         Oranjestad
        </a>
        (33,000 in 2006), divided in two districts
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Paradera" title="Paradera">
         Paradera
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/San_Nicolaas" title="San Nicolaas">
         San Nicolaas
        </a>
        , divided in two districts
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz,_Aruba" title="Santa Cruz, Aruba">
         Santa Cruz
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Savaneta" title="Savaneta">
         Savaneta
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Fauna">
        Fauna
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aruba&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Fauna">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg">
          <img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/>
         </a>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          <b>
           This section needs expansion
          </b>
          .
          <small>
           You can help by
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Aruba&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">
            adding to it
           </a>
           .
          </small>
          <small>
           <i>
            (January 2015)
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The island of Aruba, being isolated from the main land of South America, has fostered the evolution of multiple endemic animals. The island provides a habitat for the endemic
       <a href="/wiki/Cnemidophorus_arubensis" title="Cnemidophorus arubensis">
        Aruban Whiptail
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Crotalus_durissus_unicolor" title="Crotalus durissus unicolor">
        Aruba Rattlesnake
       </a>
       , as well as an endemic subspecies of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Athene_cunicularia" title="Athene cunicularia">
        Burrowing Owl
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eupsittula_pertinax" title="Eupsittula pertinax">
        Brown-throated Parakeet
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The rattlesnake and the owl are printed on the Aruban
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aruban_Florin" title="Aruban Florin">
        currency
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Flora">
        Flora
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aruba&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Flora">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aruba_Cacti.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6000" data-file-width="4000" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Aruba_Cacti.jpg/220px-Aruba_Cacti.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Aruba_Cacti.jpg/330px-Aruba_Cacti.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Aruba_Cacti.jpg/440px-Aruba_Cacti.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aruba_Cacti.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Yatu cactus growing in Aruba
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg">
          <img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/>
         </a>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          <b>
           This section needs expansion
          </b>
          .
          <small>
           You can help by
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Aruba&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">
            adding to it
           </a>
           .
          </small>
          <small>
           <i>
            (October 2015)
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The flora of Aruba differs from the typical tropical island vegetation.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Xeric_scrublands" title="Xeric scrublands">
        Xeric scrublands
       </a>
       are common, with various forms of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cacti" title="Cacti">
        cacti
       </a>
       , thorny shrubs and evergreens. The most known plant is the
       <a href="/wiki/Aloe_vera" title="Aloe vera">
        Aloe vera
       </a>
       , which has a place on the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coat_of_Arms_of_Aruba" title="Coat of Arms of Aruba">
        Coat of Arms of Aruba
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aruba&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Climate">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Climate_of_Aruba" title="Climate of Aruba">
        Climate of Aruba
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       By the
       <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">
        Köppen climate classification
       </a>
       , Aruba has a
       <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate#Hot_semi-arid_climates" title="Semi-arid climate">
        hot semi-arid climate
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">
        Köppen
       </a>
       <i>
        BSh
       </i>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-extremes_12-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-extremes-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Mean monthly temperature in Oranjestad varies little from 26.7 °C (80.1 °F) to 29.2 °C (84.6 °F), moderated by constant
       <a href="/wiki/Trade_winds" title="Trade winds">
        trade winds
       </a>
       from the Atlantic Ocean, which come from the north-east. Yearly rainfall barely exceeds 470 millimetres or 18.5 inches in Oranjestad, although it is extremely variable
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and can range from as little as 150 millimetres or 5.91 inches during strong
       <a href="/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o" title="El Niño">
        El Niño
       </a>
       years (e.g. 1911/1912, 1930/1931, 1982/1983, 1997/1998) to over 1,000 millimetres or 39.37 inches in
       <a href="/wiki/La_Ni%C3%B1a" title="La Niña">
        La Niña
       </a>
       years like 1933/1934, 1970/1971 or 1988/1989.
      </p>
      <div style="width:75%">

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">
        Demographics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aruba&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Demographics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Aruba" title="Demographics of Aruba">
        Demographics of Aruba
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aruba-demography.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="426" data-file-width="724" height="206" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Aruba-demography.png/350px-Aruba-demography.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Aruba-demography.png/525px-Aruba-demography.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Aruba-demography.png/700px-Aruba-demography.png 2x" width="350"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aruba-demography.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Population of Aruba 1961–2003, according to the
         <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Agriculture_Organization" title="Food and Agriculture Organization">
          FAO
         </a>
         in 2005; number of inhabitants given in thousands
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The population is estimated to be 75% mixed
       <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">
        European
       </a>
       /
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amerindian" title="Amerindian">
        Amerindian
       </a>
       /
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Africa" title="Ethnic groups in Africa">
        African
       </a>
       , 15%
       <a href="/wiki/Afro-Aruban" title="Afro-Aruban">
        Black
       </a>
       and 10% other ethnicities.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Arawak heritage is stronger on Aruba than on most Caribbean islands. Although no full-blooded
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Native_American_(Americas)" title="Native American (Americas)">
        Aboriginals
       </a>
       remain, the features of the islanders clearly indicate their genetic
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arawak_peoples" title="Arawak peoples">
        Arawak
       </a>
       heritage. Most of the population is descended from Caquetio Indians and Dutch and to a lesser extent of Africans, Spanish, Portuguese, English, French, and Sephardic Jewish ancestors. Aruba is a home of
       <a href="/wiki/Indo-Caribbeans" title="Indo-Caribbeans">
        Indo Caribbeans
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Javanese_Surinamese" title="Javanese Surinamese">
        Javanese
       </a>
       , who descend largely from workers contracted from India and the island of
       <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">
        Java
       </a>
       in the former
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">
        Dutch East Indies
       </a>
       (modern
       <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">
        Indonesia
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       Recently, there has been substantial immigration to the island from neighboring American and Caribbean nations, possibly attracted by the higher paid jobs. In 2007, new immigration laws were introduced to help control the growth of the population by restricting
       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_worker" title="Foreign worker">
        foreign workers
       </a>
       to a maximum of three years residency on the island.
      </p>
      <p>
       Demographically, Aruba has felt the impact of its proximity to Venezuela. Many of Aruba's families are descended from Venezuelan immigrants. There is a seasonal increase of Venezuelans living in second homes.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Language">
        Language
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aruba&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Language">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Aruba" title="Languages of Aruba">
        Languages of Aruba
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The official languages are
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">
        Dutch
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Papiamento" title="Papiamento">
        Papiamento
       </a>
       . Papiamento is the predominant language on Aruba. It is a
       <a href="/wiki/Creole_language" title="Creole language">
        creole language
       </a>
       , spoken on Aruba,
       <a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">
        Bonaire
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Curaçao">
        Curaçao
       </a>
       , that incorporates words from Portuguese, West African languages, Dutch, and Spanish. English is known by many; its usage has grown due to tourism. Other common languages spoken, based on the size of their community, are Portuguese, Chinese, German, Spanish, and French.
      </p>
      <p>
       In recent years, the government of Aruba has shown an increased interest in acknowledging the cultural and historical importance of its native language. Although spoken Papiamento is fairly similar among the several Papiamento-speaking islands, there is a big difference in written Papiamento. The orthography differs per island and even per group of people. Some are more oriented towards Portuguese and use the equivalent spelling (e.g. "y" instead of "j"), where others are more oriented towards Dutch.
      </p>
      <p>
       The book
       <i>
        The Buccaneers of America
       </i>
       , first published in 1678, states through eyewitness account that the natives on Aruba spoke Spanish already. Spanish became an important language in the 18th century due to the close economic ties with Spanish colonies in what are now Venezuela and Colombia,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and several
       <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">
        Venezuelan
       </a>
       TV networks are received. The oldest government official statement written in Papiamento dates from 1803. Around 12.6% of the population today speaks Spanish.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_16-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cia-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Aruba has four newspapers published in Papiamento:
       <i>
        Diario
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Bon Dia
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Solo di Pueblo
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        Awe Mainta
       </i>
       ; and three in English:
       <i>
        Aruba Daily
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Aruba Today
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        The News
       </i>
       .
       <i>
        Amigoe
       </i>
       is a newspaper published in Dutch. Aruba also has 18 radio stations (two AM and 16 FM) and two local television stations (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Telearuba" title="Telearuba">
        Telearuba
       </a>
       , and Channel 22).
      </p>
      <h3>

      <p>
       Three-quarters of the population is Roman Catholic.
      </p>
      <h3>

        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
